SUBJECT:
Citywide Street Rehabilitation Package 3B – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with WRECO for design services in the amount not to exceed $310,000; establish a contingency 
reserve of $31,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented 
and approve amendments within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
WRECO was selected through a qualification process using a request for proposals (RFP) for on-call pavement design 
services. A specific proposal for design services was requested from WRECO for the City’s Citywide Street Rehabilitation 
Package 3B project, which is part of the City’s Pavement Management Program. In addition, WRECO has previously 
provided engineering design services for the Citywide Street Rehabilitation Package 1C, and staff are satisfied with the 
services provided for the project. WRECO’s proposed scope, schedule, and budget all align with the City’s needs and staff 
recommends entering a contract with WRECO to perform the design services for this project for an amount not to exceed 
$310,000 and establish a contingency of $31,000 (10% of the contract budget) to cover any unforeseen changes during the 
design process. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the Citywide Street Rehabilitation Package 2/Street Rehabilitation Phase 3-B project to 
award this agreement and the contingency reserve. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This professional services agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not 
cause a physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065). The project to be designed is 
categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, maintenance, 
permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, mechanical equipment, 
or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CPI or 3%, whichever is lower.

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION 
 
 
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw. 
 
 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties. 
 
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION 
 
 
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

PROJECT DESCRIPTION 
CONSULTANT’s proposed scope of services includes designing and preparing the 
construction contract documents for the Citywide Street Rehabilitation 3B Project 
(Project). The following streets and limits are included in this scope of services.

SCOPE OF WORK 
TASK 1 – PROJECT MANAGEMENT AND COORDINATION 
Task 1.1 - Project Schedule 
CONSULTANT will prepare a preliminary Project schedule for the CITY’s review. The 
schedule will identify the critical path items, review times, and milestone submittals. 
CONSULTANT will update and issue the revised Project schedule as necessary. 
Task 1.2 - Project Kickoff Meeting and Initial Site Visit 
CONSULTANT will coordinate a Project Kickoff Meeting with the CITY. The purpose of 
the meeting will be to gain approval of the proposed base schedule and to identify any 
known Project issues. Meeting minutes will be prepared and distributed within five (5) 
working days of the meeting. 
 
124 of 445

--- page 125 ---
Page A-2 
Task 1.3 - Project Review Meetings (Virtual) 
The CONSULTANT Team will attend up to four (4) virtual meetings with the CITY. The 
primary purpose of each meeting will be to review comments received from each 
milestone deliverable. Two (2) meetings will be held after the 35% submittal: one (1) 
meeting to present the 35% plans and another meeting for the CITY to provide comments 
on the submittal. Similarly, there will be two (2) more meetings after the submittal of the 
70% plans, specifications, and estimate (PS&E). CONSULTANT will discuss any 
comments that require clarification from the CITY and obtain an agreement on the design 
team’s proposed methods to address the CITY’s comments. CONSULTANT will provide 
meeting minutes to the CITY and team members. Additionally, CONSULTANT will 
provide the CITY with a Project progress report and an invoice on a monthly basis.  
Task 1.4 - Bi-Weekly Meetings (Virtual) 
The CONSULTANT Team will attend up to sixteen (16) virtual meetings with the CITY. 
The primary purpose of each meeting will be to coordinate the design efforts and resolve 
any issues that arise during the design process. 
Task 1.5 - Quality Control 
CONSULTANT’s designated Quality Assurance/Quality Control (QA/QC) Manager will 
ensure the QA/QC procedures established for the Project will adhere to by the 
CONSULTANT. The following QC procedures will be used in the development of the 
planning and engineering documents for the Project: 
• Define key team members and their respective roles and responsibilities for the 
Project. 
• Identify, categorize, and incorporate correspondence, memoranda, and reports 
prepared for the Project within a distinct filing system that enables quick recovery 
upon request by the CITY and/or CONSULTANT Team members. 
• Perform internal plan QC reviews by the Project Manager and Team Leaders to 
ensure conflicts and miscommunication do not occur. 
• Perform QA reviews by senior management who are not involved with the 
development of the Project documents at the 70%, and 100% PS&E milestones 
before submittal to the CITY. 
 
Task 1 Deliverables 
• Project Schedule 
• Project Meeting Minutes 
• Monthly Invoices and Progress Reports 
 
 
 
125 of 445

--- page 126 ---
Page A-3 
TASK 2 – PRE-DESIGN INVESTIGATIONS 
Task 2.1 - Field Reconnaissance & Investigation 
CONSULTANT will conduct extensive field reconnaissance to assess the existing 
pavement conditions and note locations of the existing utility manholes and valve covers. 
Existing Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA) ramps will be field measured, and ramp 
slopes will be calculated to ensure that each ramp is ADA compliant. Existing curbs and 
gutters in need of repair will also be documented. 
Task 2.2 - Curb Ramp & Street Assessment Report 
CONSULTANT will prepare the Curb Ramp & Street Assessment Report for each curb 
ramp and gutter flow lines within the street section improvement limits. The report will 
assess each curb ramp and provide proposed solutions required to meet the ADA design 
criteria and provide a visual assessment of the existing gutters to identify locations of low 
spots that would create ponding. 
Task 2.3 - Topographical Survey 
CONSULTANT will perform a field survey, taking survey data points at the top of curb, 
flow line, lip of gutter, and back of sidewalk at each curb ramp location for the following 
intersections anticipating curb ramp improvements associated with the mill and overlay 
improvement only: 
• 1st Avenue @ Claremont (2 curb ramps) 
• 1st Avenue @ Delaware Street (2 curb ramps) 
• 5th Avenue @ Eldorado Street (4 curb ramps) 
• 5th Avenue @ Grant Street (4 curb ramps) 
• 5th Avenue @ Humboldt Street (4 curb ramps) 
• Alhambra Road @ 5th Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• Alhambra Road @ Maple Street (2 curb ramps) 
• B Street @ 5th Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• B Street @ 6th Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• B Street @ 7th Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• B Street @ 9th Avenue (1 curb ramp) 
• Concar Drive @ Delaware Street (2 curb ramps) 
• Delaware Street @ Charles Lane (2 curb ramps) 
• Fremont Street @ 2nd Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• Fremont Street @ 3rd Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• Humboldt Street @ 7th Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• Humboldt Street @ 9th Avenue (2 curb ramps) 
• Monte Diablo Avenue @ Claremont Street (4 curb ramps) 
 
126 of 445

--- page 127 ---
Page A-4 
The topographic survey will also include the locations of surface visible utilities (including 
dips of inlets and manholes), utility boxes, vaults, lights, signs, fire hydrants, trees and 
their drip lines, and existing driveways in the vicinity of the curb ramps. 
The survey control will be based on the California State Plane Coordinate System, North 
American Datum of 1983 (NAD 83). The vertical control will be based on the CITY’s 
vertical datum. Topographic mapping will be created from the survey data and will be 
used as the base map for the design plans. 
Task 2.4 - Pavement Field Investigation & Pavement Assessment Report 
CONSULTANT will conduct a field investigation to visually inspect the pavement 
condition. CONSULTANT will also perform subsurface exploration for the streets that are 
projected to receive mill and overlay. 
CONSULTANT will additionally take two roadway coring samples, at each of the eleven 
streets, to a depth of up to 5 feet to determine the existing pavement depths and 
subsurface conditions at each location. The CITY will provide an encroachment permit 
(no fee to CONSULTANT) for the field work. It is assumed that traffic control will be 
required to complete the coring. The bore holes will be backfilled with cement grout or 
cold patch asphalt concrete (AC).  The following is included in this task: 
 
• Obtain a CITY encroachment permit (assumed no fee to the CONSULTANT 
Team). 
• Mark out the borings in white paint and call in USA North Utility Notification a 
minimum of 72 hours before the start of the field work. 
• Drill two (2) soil borings using solid flight augers or concrete coring and hand-
augers to completion depths of 5 feet below current grades at each of the ten street 
locations (20 total borings).  
• The existing AC and any identified base material will be measured where 
penetrated with borings. All borings will be backfilled with lean cement, and the soil 
cuttings drummed and disposed of off-site. All penetrations in the asphalt will be 
patched with an 18 inch plug of rapid setting high strength concrete dyed black. 
• Bulk samples will be retrieved from the auger cuttings as the drilling advances.  
• Recovered representative samples will be visually classified to better determine 
the engineering characteristics of the soils.  
 
The results of the field investigation will be presented in a Pavement Assessment Report.    
 
For this task, we assume the following:  
• There will be three (3) days of fieldwork. 
• The borings locations will be backfilled with lean concrete grout, and the pavement 
will be replaced with rapid setting high strength concrete. 
127 of 445

--- page 128 ---
Page A-5 
• There are no planned structural excavations (e.g. utility improvements) for the 
proposed improvements. 
• County of San Mateo boring permit is not required for borings less than 10 ft deep. 
• CONSULTANT is not responsible for performing a site-specific seismic fault study 
or fault trenching as part of our scope. CONSULTANT is not performing a 
liquefaction analysis or seismic settlement analysis as part of our scope. 
• If hazardous substances are encountered work will stop and an additional scope 
and fee will be required to address hazardous substances.  
 
Task 2.5 - Utility Investigations and Potholing 
CONSULTANT will conduct a search of potential utility owners who might have facilities 
within the Project limits. We will prepare utility request letters for the CITY to send to the 
owners requesting record drawings of their facilities or confirming they do not have any 
facilities that would be in conflict with the proposed improvements. 
A composite plan of existing utilities will be prepared based on the information received 
from the utility owners and utility information received from the CITY. Potential conflicts 
between existing utilities and the proposed roadway improvements will be identified. 
CONSULTANT will prepare a potholing plan (as needed) and discuss the proposed plan 
with the CITY.  After reaching an agreement on the potholing plan, CONSULTANT and 
its potholing contractor will positively locate utilities with up to ten (10) potholes. It is 
assumed that traffic control will be required and the field work will be completed in two (2) 
days.  
Task 2.6 - Develop Design Base Maps 
CONSULTANT will compile the design base maps in AutoCAD, utilizing the aerial map 
supplemented with topographical survey, as needed. 
Task 2.7 - Basis of Design Report 
The Basis of Design (BOD) report will document the design objectives, approaches, 
assumptions, rationale, design criteria, and considerations used for calculations and 
decisions required during design.   
 
Task 2.8 - 35% Conceptual Plans 
The 35% design plans prepared under this task will include the following: 
• Conceptual Layout Plans (Identifying project improvement limits, curb ramp 
improvements, and pavement rehabilitation requirements)

TASK 4 – 100% DESIGN SUBMITTAL 
Task 4.1 - Response to 70% Comments

EXHIBIT C 
 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE  
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease.  
 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate 
 
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT. 
 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).

--- page 135 ---
Professional Services  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Page 9 of 9 
Rev 5/20 
 
 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
 
Notice of Cancellation 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. 
 
Waiver of Subrogation 
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.   
 
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.   
 
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City. 
 
Verification of Coverage 
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

SUBJECT:
Fiber Optic Network Facilities – Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a Utility Equipment Agreement with Intermountain Infrastructure Group, LLC for the construction, installation, 
maintenance, and operation of fiber optic network facilities within the public right-of-way and authorize the Public Works 
Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form attached.
BACKGROUND:
On February 28, 2019, the Public Utilities Commission of the State of California (CPUC) granted Intermountain 
Infrastructure Group, LLC (IIG) a Certificate of Public Convenience and Necessity (CPCN) that authorizes IIG to provide full, 
facilities-based and re-sold competitive local exchange telecommunication services, such as fiber and internet, within the 
State of California (Attachment 1). IIG desires to construct, install, maintain, and operate fiber optic network facilities 
within the City of San Mateo public right-of-way to provide the telecommunication services to San Mateo residents and 
clients. 
In addition to the CPUC, the City has the authority to regulate the terms and conditions for IIG’s use of the public right-of-
way, and a Utility Equipment Agreement (Attachment 2) is required. The Utility Equipment Agreement will authorize 
telecommunication services under applicable federal and state law. However, the Utility Equipment Agreement will not 
authorize cable (TV) services, broadcast television service or wireless (small cell) service. The main terms and conditions of 
the Agreement are as follows:
1.
The term of the Agreement is ten (10) years from the effective date and may only be amended in writing and 
signed by both parties. 
2.
IIG shall be required to remove or relocate their facilities, without cost or expense to the City, when made 
necessary by any lawful change of grade, alignment, or width of any street, including the construction, 
maintenance, or operation of any underground facility by the City, and/or construction, maintenance, or 
operation of any other City underground or above-ground facilities. 
3.

services.

DECISION GRANTING INTERMOUNTAIN INFRASTRUCTURE GROUP, LLC 
A CERTIFICATE OF PUBLIC CONVENIENCE AND NECESSITY IN ORDER

Summary 
Pursuant to Public Utilities (Pub. Util.) Code Section 1001, we grant 
Intermountain Infrastructure Group, LLC (Intermountain or Applicant) a 
certificate of public convenience and necessity to provide 1) full facilities-based 
and resold competitive local exchange telecommunications services; and 2) full 
facilities-based and resold interexchange service in California subject to the terms 
and conditions set forth in the Ordering Paragraphs. 
This proceeding is closed.

--- page 139 ---
A.18-05-021  ALJ/ZZ1/eg3 
 
 
 
 
- 2 - 
1. Background 
On May 23, 2018, Intermountain Infrastructure Group, LLC, a corporation 
authorized to do business in California, filed an application for a certificate of 
public convenience and necessity (CPCN) to provide: 1) full facilities-based and  
resold competitive telecommunications services in the service territories of 
Pacific Bell Telephone Company d/b/a AT&T California (AT&T California), 
Frontier California Inc.  (Frontier California)1, Citizens Telecommunications 
Company of California, Inc. d/b/a Frontier Communications of California 
(Frontier Communications), and Consolidated Communications of California 
Company (Consolidated Communications, formerly SureWest Telephone);2 and 
2) full facilities-based and resold interexchange service in California.  
Intermountain proposes to provide “infrastructure facilities (such as 
conduit and dark or lit fiber) for use in connection with the transport and 
transmission of communications.”3  If existing facilities are not available or 
economical, Intermountain may install fiber, construct new manholes and/or 
new poles.4  
Intermountain’s principal place of business is located at 533 Airport Blvd., 
Suite 400, Burlingame, California 94010.   
                                              
1  Frontier California was formerly Verizon California, Inc. (Verizon).  As of April 1, 2016, 
Verizon’s operations in California were acquired and are now operated by Frontier California, 
Inc., pursuant to Decision (D.) 15-12-005.   
2  SureWest Telephone was acquired by Consolidated Communications Inc. in 2012, pursuant to 
D.12-06-004, and SureWest Telephone changed its name to Consolidated Communications of 
California Company as of January 1, 2016. 
3  Application at 1. 
4  Response of Intermountain Infrastructure Group, LLC to Assigned ALJ Ruling, Jan. 4, 2019, 
at  2.

On October 19, 2018, the assigned Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) issued 
Administrative Law Judge’s Ruling Directing the Filing of Additional Information, to 
which Intermountain responded on October 22, 2018.  A prehearing conference 
was held on October 24, 2018.  The November 15, 2018 scoping memo and ruling 
included additional questions regarding Intermountain’s need for full 
facilities-based authority and the lack of a proposed tariff.  On November 19, 
2018, Intermountain responded to the scoping memo and ruling.  Due to the 
need for details regarding Intermountain’s business, the lack of a proposed tariff, 
and the proponent’s environmental assessment, on January 3, 2019, the ALJ 
issued a second Administrative Law Judge’s Ruling Directing the Filing of Additional 
Information.  On January 4, 2019, Intermountain responded.   
2. Jurisdiction 
Public Utilities Code (Pub. Util. Code) § 216(a) defines the term “Public 
utility” to include a “telephone corporation,” which in turn is defined in Public 
Utilities Code § 234(a) as “every corporation or person owning, controlling, 
operating, or managing any telephone line for compensation within this state.”  
Intermountain proposes to provide infrastructure facilities, such as conduit 
and dark or lit fiber infrastructure, in connection with the transport and 
transmission of communications. Intermountain will use existing conduit, poles, 
and infrastructure if feasible and economical, but will build new facilities if 
required to serve customers.  For example, Intermountain may “construct 
underground facilities of longer length to provide services to schools, 
government office buildings, or business customers who have needs for new or 
140 of 445

--- page 141 ---
A.18-05-021  ALJ/ZZ1/eg3 
 
 
 
 
- 4 - 
additional telecommunications bandwidth.”5  Intermountain is a telephone 
corporation and a public utility subject to our jurisdiction. 
Intermountain states even though it does not expect to operate as an 
interstate Common Carrier, to the extent it engages in operations as a Common 
Carrier as defined by § 153 of the Federal Telecommunications Act of 1996 (Act), 
it will be eligible to interconnect with the public switched telephone network 
pursuant to § 251 and § 252 of the Act,6 and that if granted a CPCN, it will 
operate as a telephone corporation under Pub. Util. Code § 234(a), and obey the 
Pub. Util. Code and all Commission rules, decisions, and orders applicable to 
telephone corporations.7  
3. California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Pursuant to CEQA and Rule 2.48 of the Commission’s Rules of Practice and 
Procedure, the Commission examines projects to determine any potential 
environmental impacts in order that adverse effects are avoided and 
environmental quality is restored or enhanced to the fullest extent possible under 
CEQA.

In the Proponent’s Environmental Assessment, Intermountain’s proposed 
construction activities will generally include the installation of “relatively short 
conduit routes, installations of [] poles where existing facilities are inadequate, 
and installation or construction of other, small above-ground facilities.”9  The 
construction “would occur in existing roadways or other previously-developed 
and disturbed rights-of-way.”  Intermountain’s proposed activities include: 
- Installing fiber to link customers to existing conduits; 
- Constructing a new manhole and/or short conduit stub when 
necessary; 
- Installing overlash cabling between existing utility poles; 
- Constructing new poles when necessary; and 
- Constructing underground facilities to lay its own conduit 
when necessary.10 
Intermountain expects its activities to fall within one or more categorical 
CEQA exemptions, but at this time, it cannot identify the specific projects, sites, 
or routes of construction.11   Intermountain requests approval to utilize a 
procedure for expedited CEQA review of its projects once it is aware of a specific 
site(s) and route(s) which it plans construction.   
It is possible that Intermountain’s activities will fall within one or more of 
the categorical exemptions under CEQA.  Intermountain’s proposed procedure 
for expedited review tracks the expedited review procedure that we have 
approved for other carriers.  Such a process will expedite CEQA review and is

appropriate for the type of construction outlined here, which may be

At the same time, the proposed CEQA review process will enable Intermountain

We have reviewed the application and Intermountain’s 
responses to ALJ’s rulings and find that: 
 Intermountain’s proposed facilities-based project activities are 
very limited; 
 These activities would in almost all circumstances be very

 The proposed process for reviewing the applicability of CEQA

service without the delay or burden of a full CEQA review

We therefore approve Intermountain’s proposed process for Commission 
review of claimed CEQA exemptions for construction projects undertaken 
pursuant to Intermountain’s full facilities-based authority, based on the specific 
facts of this case with the following modifications related to the Commission’s

seeking the requisite approval and full CEQA review, before commencing any 
construction activities. 
Intermountain shall not perform any full facilities-based construction 
activities without first obtaining an NTP from the Energy Division or 
authorization by the Commission after the requisite environmental review.

technologically advanced telecommunications services within the state.

4. Financial Qualifications 
To be granted a CPCN, an applicant for authority to provide full facilities-
based resold competitive local exchange and interexchange services must 
demonstrate that it has a minimum of $100,000 cash or cash equivalent, 
reasonably liquid and readily available to meet the firm’s start-up expenses.13  
An applicant must also demonstrate that it has sufficient additional resources 
to cover all deposits required by local exchange carriers and/or interexchange 
carriers in order to provide the proposed service.14  Applicant provided 
Exhibit F, which contains the Guarantee of Jeffrey Yount, the CEO of 
Intermountain.  Mr. Yount guarantees that $100,000 would be available to 
Intermountain for one year following certification, plus $20,000 to cover the 
deposit required by AT&T California, Frontier California, Frontier 
Communications, and Consolidated Communications.  In addition, 
Intermountain submitted financial information of an investment account held at 
Stifel Bank and Trust with a certification by Mr. Yount that the funds will be

14  The requirement for Competitive Local Carrier (CLC) applicants to demonstrate that they

Intermountain has provided documentation that it has the funds available

additional resources are required at this time to cover deposits.

6. Tariffs 
Intermountain asserts a tariff is not required because it “will provide 
services and facilities on an individually-negotiated contract basis.”19  
Intermountain “will not provide switched access service or basic single-line 
residential service.”20  In effect, Intermountain requests detariffed status.   
Because Intermountain is not providing residential local service at this 
time, Intermountain may be exempt from the requirement to file tariffs.   
In the future, if Intermountain decides to offer services that require a tariff, 
such as local exchange services for residential customers, Intermountain must 
submit proposed tariffs and/or user guides to the Communications Division via 
Tier 2 advice letters using the GO 96-B advice letter process before initiation of 
service.  Furthermore, Intermountain shall comply with the consumer protection 
rules identified in D.98-08-031.

under Pub. Util. Code § 1001, provide a statement regarding GO 104-A, Section 2.

required of a public utility under Commission jurisdiction.

Intermountain estimates it will serve ten customers during the first year of 
operation and 50 customers during the fifth year of operation.23  Therefore, 
Intermountain has complied with this requirement. 
10. Request for Treatment as a Non-dominant Carrier 
Applicant requests treatment as a non-dominant interexchange carrier 
(NDIEC) by stating it “will operate as a non-dominant carrier.”24  Applicant is a 
“small start-up” and “will compete against large established carriers such as 
AT&T California, Frontier California, AT&T Communications, CenturyLink, and 
others having far greater financial resources and established customer bases.”25

As an NDIEC, Applicant requests exemption from the requirements of 
Pub. Util. Code §§ 816 – 830 concerning stocks and security and § 851 concerning 
the encumbrance and transfer of utility property.26  While the Commission has 
granted exemption from §§ 816 – 830 to others, exemption from §§ 851 – 854 is 
not commonly granted and an exception is not warranted here. The Commission 
detailed its rules regarding exemption of non-dominant carriers in D.85-01-008, 
and subsequently modified in D.85-07-081 and D.85-11-044.  We grant 
Applicant’s request for non-dominant interexchange carrier status, which 
provides an exemption from Pub. Util. Code §§ 816 – 830 concerning stocks and 
security, provided that it follows all rules detailed in the above referenced 
decisions.27 
11. Safety Considerations 
With the adoption of the Safety Policy Statement of the California Public 
Utilities Commission on July 10, 2014, the Commission has, among other things, 
heightened its focus on the potential safety implications of every proceeding.  We 
have considered the potential safety implications here.  The Commission is 
satisfied that Intermountain will meet the Commission’s minimum safety goals 
and expectations of competitive local exchange carriers (CLECs) because: 
1) Intermountain has taken steps to meet the financial requirements as set forth 
in this decision for a facilities-based CLEC, and 2) Intermountain is a public 
utility that is required pursuant to Pub. Util. Code § 451 to “… furnish and 
maintain such adequate, efficient, just and reasonable service, instrumentalities, 
equipment, and facilities, including telephone facilities …  as are necessary to

promote the safety, health, comfort, and convenience of its patrons, employees, 
and the public.”   
12. Conclusion 
We conclude that the application conforms to our rules for certification as 
a competitive local exchange and interexchange carrier.  Accordingly, we grant 
intermountain 1) full facilities-based and resold competitive telecommunications 
services in the service territories of AT&T California, Frontier California, Frontier 
Communications, and Consolidated Communications; and 2) full facilities-based 
and resold interexchange service in California subject to compliance with the 
terms and conditions set forth in the Ordering Paragraphs. 
The CPCN granted by this decision provides benefits to Intermountain 
and corresponding obligations.  Intermountain receives authority to operate in 
the prescribed service territory, and this authority enables Intermountain, 
pursuant to section 251 of the 1934 Communications Act, as amended by the 
1996 Telecommunications Act (47 U.S.C. § 251), to interconnect with 
telecommunications carriers.28  This authority also enables Intermountain to 
obtain access to public rights-of-way in California as set forth in D.98-10-058, 
subject to the CEQA requirements set forth in this decision.   
In return, Intermountain shall comply with all Public Utilities Code 
provisions, Commission rules, General Orders, and decisions applicable to 
telephone corporations providing approved services.  The applicable statutes, 
rules, General Orders, and decisions include, but are not limited to consumer 
                                              
28  The California Public Utilities Code uses the term “telephone corporation.”  Its counterpart in 
federal law is a “telecommunications carrier.”   
 
152 of 445

--- page 153 ---
A.18-05-021  ALJ/ZZ1/eg3 
 
 
 
 
- 16 - 
protection rules, tariffing, and reporting requirements.  Moreover, Intermountain 
shall pay all Commission prescribed user fees and public purpose program 
surcharges as set forth in the Appendix B of this decision, comply with CEQA, 
and adhere to Pub. Util. Code § 451 which states that every public utility “…shall 
furnish and maintain such adequate, efficient, just, and reasonable service, 
instrumentalities, equipment, and facilities, including telephone facilities, as 
defined in § 54.1 of the Civil Code, as are necessary to promote the safety, health, 
comfort, and convenience of its patrons, employees, and the public.” 
13. Request to File Under Seal 
Pursuant to Rule 11.4 of the Commission’s Rules of Practice and 
Procedure, Intermountain has filed motions for leave to file Exhibit F, the 
financial documentation supporting the application, as confidential materials 
under seal.  Intermountain represents that the information is sensitive, and 
disclosure could place Intermountain at an unfair business disadvantage.  We 
have granted similar requests in the past and do so here.  
14. Categorization and Need for Hearings  
In Resolution ALJ 176-3417, dated May 31, 2018, the Commission 
preliminarily categorized this application as ratesetting, and preliminarily 
determined that an evidentiary hearing is necessary.  On October 24, 2018, the 
assigned ALJ held a pre-hearing conference.  On November 15, 2018, the 
assigned Commissioner issued the Scoping Memo and Ruling choosing to not 
disturb the preliminary determination that an evidentiary hearing is necessary.  
No protests have been received.  There is no apparent reason why the application 
should not be granted.  Given these developments, this decision now concludes 
that an evidentiary hearing is not necessary.

requested.  Accordingly, pursuant to § 311(g)(2) of the Pub. Util. Code and

more CEQA categorical exemptions.

have a significant adverse effect upon the environment.

is reasonably liquid and readily available to meet its start-up expenses.

deposits that may be required by other telephone corporations in order to 
provide the proposed service.

and technical expertise to provide local exchange services to the public.

Conclusions of Law 
1. Intermountain should be granted a CPCN to provide 1) full facilities-based 
and resold competitive telecommunications services in the service territories of 
AT&T California, Frontier California, Frontier Communications, and 
Consolidated Communications; and 2) full facilities-based and resold 
interexchange service in California, subject to the terms and conditions set forth 
in the Ordering Paragraphs. 
2. Intermountain should be allowed to use the Energy Division 21-day CEQA 
exemption process.   
3. Intermountain, once granted a CPCN, should be subject to the applicable 
Commission rules, decisions, General Orders, and statutes that pertain to 
California public utilities.  
4. Intermountain should be granted an exemption from the requirement to 
file tariffs. 
5. Intermountain’s motion to file under seal its Exhibit F to the application, 
should be granted for three years.

O R D E R  
IT IS ORDERED that:  
1. A certificate of public convenience and necessity is granted to 
Intermountain to provide 1) full facilities-based and resold competitive 
telecommunications services in the service territories of AT&T California, 
Frontier California, Frontier Communications, and Consolidated 
Communications, formerly SureWest Telephone; and 2) full facilities-based and 
resold interexchange service in California, subject to the terms and conditions set 
forth below. 
2. In the event Intermountain decides to offer services that require a tariff, 
such as local exchange services for residential customers, Intermountain must 
submit proposed tariffs and/or user guides to the Communications Division via 
Tier 2 advice letters using the General Order 96-B advice letter process before 
initiation of service.   
3. The corporate identification number assigned to Intermountain, U7355C, 
must be included in the caption of all original filings with this Commission, and 
in the titles of other pleadings filed in existing cases. 
4. Intermountain must file, in this docket, a written acceptance of the 
certificate granted in this proceeding within 30 days of the effective date of this 
decision.  Written acceptance filed in this docket does not reopen the proceeding. 
5. The certificate granted by this decision will expire if not exercised within 
12 months of the effective date of this decision.

Intermountain a letter which states the specific reasons that the claimed 
California Environmental Quality Act exemptions do not apply to the proposed

An original and a machine readable, copy using Microsoft Word and Excel, or 
compatible format must be submitted to the California Public Utilities 
Commission, State Office Building, 505 Van Ness Avenue, Room 3107, 
San Francisco, CA  94102-3298, no later than May 1st of the year following the

1. 
 Each utility must list and provide the following information for 
each affiliated entity and regulated subsidiary that the utility had during the 
period covered by the Annual Affiliate Transaction Report. 
 Form of organization (e.g., corporation, partnership, joint 
venture, strategic alliance, etc.); 
 Brief description of business activities engaged in; 
 Relationship to the utility (e.g., controlling corporation, 
subsidiary, regulated subsidiary, affiliate);

ownership)

 Corporate officers. 
2.

showing any and all corporate relationships between the utility and its affiliated 
entities and regulated subsidiaries in #1 above.  The chart must have the 
controlling corporation (if any) at the top of the chart, the utility and any 
subsidiaries and/or affiliates of the controlling corporation in the middle levels 
of the chart, and all secondary subsidiaries and affiliates (e.g., a subsidiary that in 
turn is owned by another subsidiary and/or affiliate) in the lower levels.  Any 
regulated subsidiary must be clearly noted.

UTILITY EQUIPMENT AGREEMENT BETWEEN THE CITY OF SAN  MATEO AND  IIG  FOR
THE CONSTRUCTION,  INSTALLATION,  MAINTENANCE, AND  OPERATION  OF FIBER
OPTIC  NETWORK FACILITIES WITHIN THE  PUBLIC  RIGHT-OF-WAY
This Agreement ("Agreement")  is dated for identification this             of
2021,  by and  between the CITY OF SAN  MATEO,  a  municipal
corporation (herein termed "CITY"),  and  lntermountain  Infrastructure Group,  LLC,  a
Delaware limited  liability company  (herein termed  "IIG").
RECITALS
WHEREAS,  llG  has a certificate of qualification to do business in the State of
California;  and
WHEREAS,  llG  is authorized to provide telecommunication services in the State
of California  by the  Public Utilities Commission  of the  State of California  (herein termed
PUC);  and
WHEREAS,  llG desires to construct, install, and maintain Fiber Optic Network
Facilities within the  Public Right-of-Way within  CITY;  and
WH EREAS, CITY has the authority to regulate the terms and conditions for the
use of Public Right-of-\/Vay for the construction, installation, and maintenance of Fiber
Optic Network Facilities by private telecommunication services providers; and
NOW, THEREFORE,  in consideration of the recitals and the mutual promises
contained  herein,  CITY and  lIG agree as follows:
DEFINITIONS
"llG" shall  mean  lntermountain  Infrastructure Group,  LLC,  and  its  lawful  successors
or assigns.
"CITY" means the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation of the State
of   California,    and    includes   the   duly   elected    or   appointed    officers,    agents,
employees,  and volunteers of the CITY OF SAN MATEO, individually or collectively.
"Public Right-of-Way" means in,  upon,  along,  across,  and  under the public
streets,  ways,  alleys,  and  places,  and  including  public utility easements and  public
service easements, as the same now or may thereafter exist that are under
jurisdiction  of or controlled  by said  CITY.
Utility Equipment Agreement between the City of San  Mateo and  llG
Page  1  of 12
173 of 445

--- page 174 ---
"Fiber Optic Network Facilities" or "Facilities" means llG fiber optic cables,
coaxial,  Ethernet and copper cables, conduits,  converters, splice boxes,
cabinets,  handholes,  manholes,  vaults,  equipment,  drains,  surface location
markers,  appurtenances,  and related facilities located or to be located in the
Public Right-of-Way of CITY and used or useful for the transmission of
telecommunications.
"Telecommunications Services" means all communications services  llG  is
permitted to provide under applicable federal and state law, except that this
Agreement does not authorize llG to provide cable (TV) services as such term is
defined  in 47 U.S.C.  § 522,  broadcast television service or wireless (cell) service.
LIMITATIONS AND  RESTRICTIONS_
1.    CITY hereby grants authorization to llG,  subject to reservations,
covenants,  and conditions herein contained, to construct,  reconstruct,  install,
reinstall,  maintain and operate,  replace,  relocate,  and  remove Fiber Optic Network
Facilities used for Telecommunications Services within  Public Right-of-Way
located within the corporate limits of the CITY OF SAN  MATEO,  subject to
obtaining  all required  permits and approvals.
2.    This Agreement is not a grant by CITY of any property interest but is
made subject and subordinate to the prior and continuing right of CITY and its
assigns to use all  Public Right-of-Way jn the performance of its duty,  including,
but not limited to,  public use as a street and for the purpose of laying,  installing,
maintaining,  repairing,  protecting,  replacing,  and  removing sanitary sewers,
water mains, storm drains, gas mains,  poles,  overhead and underground electric
and telephone wires,  electroliers,  cable television,  and other utility and  municipal
uses together with appurtenances thereof and with right of ingress and egress,
along, over, across and in said Public Right-of-Way; provided, however, should lIG
be required to relocate its Fiber Optic Network Facilities due to the actions of any
nongovernmental third  party,  such third party shall  be required to reimburse llG
for its full cost of such relocation and lIG shall not be required to relocate its facilities
until it receives an executed reimbursement agreement from the
nongovernmental third party, unless removal is required to protect or preserve the
public health, safety, welfare or interest.
3.    This Agreement is made subject to all easements,  restrictions,  conditions,
covenants, encumbrances, and claims of title which may affect said Public Right-of-
Way,  and  it is understood that llG,  at its own cost and expense,  shall obtain such
permission as may be necessary consistent with any other existing  rights.
4.    The construction,  installation,  operation,  maintenance,  and  removal of said
Fiber Optic Network Facilities shall  be accomplished without cost or expense to
CITY subject to the approval of CITY's Public Works  Director in such a manner as
not to endanger personnel or property, or unreasonably obstruct travel on any road,
walk or other access thereon within said  Public Right-of-Way.
COMPLIANCE WITH  STANDARDS
5.    IIG shall at all times during the duration of this Agreement maintain said
Utility Equipment Agreement between the City of San  Mateo and  llG
Page 2 of 12
174 of 445

--- page 175 ---
Fiber Optic Network Facilities in good and safe condition  and free from any
nuisance to the satisfaction of CITY's Public Works Director.

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
July 19, 2021 
SUBJECT:
California Department of Transportation Sustainable Transportation Planning Grant Program – Grant Funding and 
Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the acceptance of grant funding with the California Department of Transportation for the 
Sustainable Transportation Planning Grant Program and authorize the City Manager to execute a funding agreement and 
any necessary documents.
BACKGROUND:
The California Department of Transportation (Caltrans) released a call for projects in Summer 2020 for the fiscal year 2021-
22 Sustainable Transportation Planning Grant Program. The program funds projects that support sustainable communities’ 
strategies, the goals and best practices in the California Transportation Commission’s Regional Transportation Plan 
Guidelines, and help to achieve the State's greenhouse gas reduction targets. 
The Public Works Department, Community Development Department, and the City Manager's Office jointly prepared a 
grant application in the amount of $490,882 for the development of the San Mateo Complete Streets Plan. City Council 
approved a letter of support to accompany the application at its February 1, 2021 meeting. The Complete Streets Plan is 
intended to complement the City’s ongoing General Plan Update by creating an actionable transportation plan that 
considers safety for all modes of transportation and results in policies, goals, and prioritized projects that improve 
mobility, equity, connectivity, and sustainability. The Complete Streets Plan will combine existing transportation and 
related plans with a data-driven safety analysis to identify priority areas and projects in the City to implement a cohesive, 
safe transportation network for all users. 
Caltrans notified City staff in June 2021 that the grant application was recommended for funding. Staff recommends City 
Council adopt the Resolution as required by Caltrans to authorize the City Manager to execute a funding agreement 
necessary to receive the grant funding. Caltrans has not yet provided the proposed funding agreement; staff will review 
the proposed agreement and any related documents when received. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact for adopting this resolution. There is a required minimum 11.47% local match ($94,621) , and 
sufficient Measure A funds are available to fulfill the required local match.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, because preparation of the San Mateo Complete Streets Plan does not 
involve a commitment to construct a specific project and it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

Agenda Number:  16
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
File ID: 21-4592
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
July 19, 2021 
SUBJECT:
Natural Gas Line Replacement and Improvements – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Award an agreement to EPS, Inc. dba Express Plumbing for construction of the Natural Gas Line Replacement and 
Improvements Project in an amount not to exceed $250,711; establish a contingency reserve in an amount of $25,000; and 
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders 
within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Natural Gas Line Replacement and Improvements Project (Project) is part of the Clean Water Program’s (CWP) efforts 
to modernize the existing Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) and maintain safe and reliable operations.  An existing 
steel natural gas line at the WWTP serves the digester heating boiler system and provides fuel for heating in the existing 
buildings. This natural gas line has reached the end of its useful life and its replacement is critical for WWTP safety and 
reliability. This Project will replace the existing natural gas line with a new 3-inch medium density polyethylene pipeline 
connecting the WWTP facilities with the Pacific Gas and Electric tie-in point. 
In accordance with Municipal Code Section 3.60.030, a competitive public process was used to obtain bids for this service. 
A Notice Inviting Sealed Proposals and Bidding Documents was issued to advertise the project on March 30, 2021. Five bids 
were received and opened on April 27, 2021 with the following results: 
Contractor
Bid Amount
EPS, Inc.
$250,711
Kingdom Pipeline
$268,461
Trinet, Inc. 
$286,321
MBS Engineering
$329,522
Kiewit Infrastructure West Inc.
$332,237
The lowest bid of $250,711 is 10.5% percent below the engineer’s estimate of $280,000. 
The City was informed the Department of Industrial Relations – Division of Labor Standards and Enforcement issued a Civil 
Penalty and Wage Assessment to the lowest bidder, EPS, Inc. (EPS), in 2020, related to alleged violations of prevailing 
wages and apprenticeship standards set by the California Labor Code. EPS submitted a Request for Review and the matter 
is currently pending. As a final determination has not been made, staff recommends awarding the contract to EPS and 
believes disqualifying a contractor based on a pending case would set an unfair precedent. EPS has performed satisfactory 
work for the City in the past and has provided all required prevailing wage documentation for those contracts.
189 of 445

--- page 190 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Based on staff’s determination that the low bid submitted is responsive and responsible, staff recommends awarding the 
agreement to EPS, Inc.

City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue

Agenda Number:  17
Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
File ID: 21-4808
TO:
City Council

Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
July 19, 2021 
SUBJECT:
Wireless Telecommunications Facilities in the Public Right-of-Way – Amended Design Standards, Application Requirements 
and Permit Fees
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the Design Standards and Application Requirements, authorize the Director of Public Works 
to make future revisions to the Design Standards, as necessary, to comply with applicable rules and laws, and amend the 
Wireless Communications Facilities Permit fee in the Adopted Comprehensive Fee Schedule for fiscal year 2021-22.
BACKGROUND:
The City introduced an ordinance for adoption to amend Chapter 17.10, “Wireless Communication Facilities in the Public 
Right-of-Way” of the San Mateo Municipal at the June 21, 2021 City Council meeting. The amendments to Chapter 17.10 
were recommended to comply with the Federal Communications Commission (FCC)’s September 26, 2018 order, FCC 18-
133, the Declaratory Ruling and Third Report and Order in the Matter of Accelerating Wireless Broadband Deployment by 
Removing Barriers to Infrastructure Investment (the “FCC Order”) regarding small cell wireless facilities deployment (i.e. 
“small cells”). 
Based on the FCC Order, effective as of January 2019, all City permits and authorizations for small cells placed on an 
existing structure must be issued within 60 days from the submittal of the application materials. The total processing time 
for small cells placed on a new or replacement structure is 90 days from submittal. Failure to meet the shot clock 
establishes a presumption that the City effectively prohibited service. 
The FCC Order and the recent Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals case Portland v. FCC, No. 18-72689 (9th Cir. Aug. 12, 2020), 
confirmed that local governments may regulate aesthetic standards for small cells but are subject to certain limitations 
and must be published in advance. 
The FCC Order requires the City make City-owned vertical infrastructure in the public right-of-way available for the 
attachment of small wireless facilities by wireless carriers. The City’s Master License Agreement grants licensees the right 
to apply for individual site licenses to install their small wireless facilities on City-owned poles in the public right-of-way, 
such as streetlight poles. The City is limited by the FCC Order to cost recovery.  Therefore, the City will use the FCC’s “safe 
harbor” rate of $270 per year for each attachment to a City-owned structure in the public right-of-way as a license fee. 
This license fee will increase by 3% annually. The FCC Order stated that fees imposed as part of the regulation of small 
wireless facilities must be (1) a reasonable approximation of the local government’s costs, (2) based only on objectively 
reasonable costs, and (3) no higher than the fees charged to similarly situated competitors in similar situations. 
Based on these recent rules and orders, the City staff amended Municipal Code Chapter 17.10 for the Council to consider 
for adoption. At the introduction of the revised ordinance, staff also indicated that if the amended ordinance is approved, 
201 of 445

--- page 202 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
the Design Standards and Application Requirements and revised Fee Schedule will require approval to be consistent with 
the recent legal requirements. 
Design Standards and Application Requirements 
The revised Design Standards and Application Requirements establish reasonable and comprehensive standards and 
procedures, including but not limited to the facilities’ siting, aesthetics, construction, operation, modification, and 
removal, for the permitting of small cells and other infrastructure deployments within the City. These design standards aim 
to promote the community’s interest of protecting the City of San Mateo’s visual character while complying with the FCC 
Order. 
It is important to note that, as a resolution rather than an ordinance, and by authorizing the Director of Public Works to 
make additional revisions to the Design Standards and Application Requirements, the City Council is allowing the 
procedures to be revised more quickly than if the contents were codified in an ordinance. This will allow the City to modify 
and adapt the policy in the future to respond to the rapidly changing law and technology related to small cells. By 
establishing revised policies and procedures, the City can continue to retain some degree of local control on the 
deployment of small cells and also enable staff to process applications within the required timeframe in accordance with 
objective aesthetic regulations required by law. 
Letters received by AT&T and Verizon just prior to the June 21, 2021 City Council meeting prompted staff to make 
additional revisions to the Design Standards and Application Requirements section of the version presented at the June 21, 
2021 meeting to highlight that the City’s regulations and preferences consider options that are technically feasible. The 
City’s response to the letters and a redlined version of the Design Standards are attached for reference. 
Revised Fee Schedule 
In accordance with the changes to federal law, the revised fees relating to the Wireless Communications Facilities Permit 
in the Comprehensive Fee Schedule also allow the City to:

Recover actual costs related to the processing of Wireless Permit applications by charging a reasonable and 
refundable deposit; 

Charge a reasonable deposit for a Master License Agreement, which is required in order to install a small cell 
wireless facility on a City pole in the right-of-way; 

Charge a reasonable safe harbor license fee of $270/per pole; 

Charge a deposit for procession Section 6409 Permit application for modifications of facilities that do not 
substantially change the physical dimensions of the existing facility; and 

Assess a reasonable hourly rate for City staff time related to processing a wireless permit in the right-of-way. 
These fees are based on a reasonable approximation of City’s actual costs associated with the processing of a Wireless 
Permit in the public right-of-way, are only assessed on objectively reasonable charges, and are non-discriminatory. 
Resolution 
The attached Resolution for consideration and adoption is thus recommended to 1) approve the revised Design Standards 
and Application Requirements; 2) authorize the Director of Public Works to make future revisions to the Design Standards, 
as necessary to comply with applicable rules and laws consistent with San Mateo Municipal Code Ch. 17.10; and 3) adopt 
an amended fee schedule for the permit and licensing fees and associated administrative costs related to wireless 
facilities. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The impact on revenue has not been fully determined. The fee is for cost recovery of staff time.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This approval of a resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, under CEQA Guidelines §15378, and it can be seen with 
certainty that it will not cause a physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
RESOLUTION NO. _____ (2021) 
 
APPROVE AMENDED DESIGN STANDARDS AND APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS FOR WIRELESS FACILITIES IN 
THE PUBLIC RIGHT OF WAY; AMEND THE WIRELESS COMMUNICATIONS FACILITIES PERMIT FEE SECTION TO 
REVISE FEES FOR WIRELESS PERMITS IN THE COMPREHENSIVE FEE SCHEDULE FOR 2021-2022 
 
WHEREAS, on July 16, 2018, the City of San Mateo adopted San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 17.10, 
"Wireless Telecommunications Facilities in the Public Right-Of-Way" to regulate wireless communication 
facilities;  
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to the City’s Municipal Code Chapter 17.10, the City Council authorizes the Director 
of Public Works to develop, publish and from time to time update or amend permit application requirements, 
forms, checklists, guidelines, informational handouts and other related materials that the Director finds 
necessary, appropriate or useful for processing any application governed under that Chapter; 
 
WHEREAS, on July 16, 2018, the City adopted by Resolution number 84, standard conditions of approval 
for wireless telecommunications permits in the public right-of-way, titled the “Design and Engineering Standards 
and Application Requirements”;   
 
WHEREAS, since that time, significant changes in federal laws that affect local authority over 
telecommunications facilities and other related infrastructure deployments in the public rights-of-way have 
occurred, including, but not limited to, the following: 
 
• 
On September 26, 2018, the FCC adopted a Declaratory Ruling and Third Report and Order, FCC 18-133 
(rel. Sep. 27, 2018) (the “Small Cell Order”), which, among many other things, creates a new regulatory 
classification for small wireless facilities, alters existing “shot clock” regulations to require local public 
agencies to act within 60 or 90 days on applications for small wireless facilities, and provides that a 
failure to act within the applicable timeframe presumptively constitutes an effective prohibition; 
 
• 
The Small Cell Order also specified safe harbor fees such as for a license to use the public right-of-way 
and also stated that fees imposed as part of the regulation of small wireless facilities must be: (1) a 
reasonable approximation of the local government’s costs, (2) based only on objectively reasonable 
costs, and (3) no higher than the fees charged to similarly-situated competitors in similar situations; 
 
• 
The Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals in Portland v. FCC, No. 18-72689 (9th Cir. Aug. 12, 2020), upheld the 
Small Cell Order and prior FCC orders except for the provisions dealing with local governments’ 
authority over aesthetic regulations. Aesthetic rules must be both reasonable and technically feasible 
based on the prior FCC Small Cell Order. 
 
WHEREAS, the significant adverse consequences for noncompliance with these changes in applicable 
law, the City Council finds that the revised aesthetic and operational regulations that supplements Chapter 
17.10 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is a necessary and appropriate means to protect the public health, 
safety and welfare from the potential harm caused by unregulated small wireless facilities and other 
infrastructure deployments in the public rights-of-way;

WHEREAS, the revised Design and Engineering Standards and Application Requirements, attached 
hereto as Exhibit “A” and incorporated herein by this reference, establishes reasonable, uniform and 
comprehensive standards and procedures for small wireless facilities and other infrastructure deployment in the 
public right-of-way, for the construction, installation, collocation, modification, operation, relocation and 
removal of such facilities within the City of San Mateo’s territorial boundaries, consistent with and to the extent 
permitted under federal and California state law;  
 
WHEREAS, the City Council wishes to set and revise fees and deposits attached hereto as Exhibit “B” and 
incorporated herein by this reference, related to licensing, permitting, and administering small cell wireless 
facilities in the City’s public right-of-way under Chapter 17.10 and the revised Design and Engineering Standards 
and Application Requirements, consistent with applicable laws; 
 
WHEREAS, the proposed fees and deposits are based on reasonable approximation of the City costs and 
staff’s actual hours spent on processing an application for a Wireless Permit under Chapter 17.10, and are thus 
reasonable, cost-based, and nondiscriminatory consistent with the FCC orders and applicable laws;

the fees are charged.

the provisions in this Resolution, revised Design Standards and Application Requirements, and Fee 
Schedule are consistent with the San Mateo Municipal Code and applicable federal and state laws; and

Schedule will be detrimental to the public interest, health, safety, convenience or welfare.

The Design Standards and Application Requirements - 2021 
Page 1 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The purpose of this document, the Design Standards and Application Requirements, is to establish requirements 
and design standards for installing wireless communication facilities in the City of San Mateo’s right-of-way 
(ROW).  The City of San Mateo seeks to permit wireless carriers to install wireless communications facilities, 
within the public right-of-way, in order to provide cellular coverage and capacity throughout the City, while 
ensuring facilities are well-maintained and do not 
significantly detract from City streetscapes. 
 
The City does not regulate the technologies 
wireless carriers use, but it does have certain 
powers to regulate the time, place, manner and 
aesthetics of wireless communications facilities.  
These design standards and requirements are 
intended to convey design preferences and 
application requirements.   
 
However, the City recommends and prefers that wireless carriers avoid pole locations where equipment would 
be in front of architecturally significant features, or in locations where they would have visual impacts of 
significance, such as residential neighborhoods, near schools and parks. 
 
Wireless providers should be made aware of the City’s preference for installation of wireless facilities on City 
owned streetlights, due to the improved aesthetic qualities of these facilities.  Wireless providers shall work 
with the City to establish a license agreement for the use of City owned streetlights. Secondly, the City 
recommends and prefers installation in areas not zoned residential, as well as near schools or parks. Residential 
areas should be considered as the last option. 
 
These requirements are meant to provide a general overview of the procedures and requirements for 
installation of wireless communications facilities on both City owned and utility poles located within the public 
right of way.  Additional conditions, information and/or procedures may be necessary based on the 
circumstances, project scope and the location being proposed by the applicant, or as deemed necessary by the 
City.   
 
San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 17.10, “Wireless Communications Facilities in the Public Right-of-Way” was 
adopted by City Council in 2021 (hereinafter the “Code”).  The abbreviations, phrases, terms and words used in 
these Design Standards and Application Requirements will have the same meanings assigned to them in Chapter 
17.10 of the Code. Undefined phrases, terms or words in this document will have the meanings assigned to 
them in 47 U.S.C. § 153, as may be amended from time to time, and, if not defined therein, will have their 
ordinary meanings. If there are any discrepancies between the standards and requirements in this document 
and the Code, the Code shall prevail. 
 
The applicant or its successors shall comply fully with all conditions specified in this document, or as modified 
by the Director of Public Works.  Failure to comply with any condition shall constitute grounds for revocation of 
an applicable permit or license.  In the event that radio frequency (RF) emissions for the site exceed Federal 
Communications Commission (FCC) standards, the applicant will be required to immediately cease and desist 
The purpose of this document is to 
establish requirements for 
installing wireless facilities in the 
City of San Mateo’s right-of-way.

operation of the facility until such time that the violation is corrected to the satisfaction of the Director of Public

Any carrier/provider authorized by the City to operate a specific wireless communications facility installation 
may assign the operation of the facility to another carrier licensed by the California Public Utilities Commission 
(CPUC) and FCC for that radio frequency provided that such transfer is made known to the City in advance of 
such operation, and all conditions of approval for the subject installation are carried out by the new 
carrier/provider. 
 
Below are requirements to aid wireless communications providers in planning facility locations and compiling 
the necessary information to obtain a Wireless Permit as provided in San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 17.10 
“Wireless Communications Facilities in the Public Right-of-Way”. Wireless communications providers are also 
directed to review and comply with all other requirements as provided in Chapter 17.10,  that can be found on 
the City’s website. 
 
Three different types of wireless facility infrastructure installations are permitted within San Mateo rights of 
way. These types include: 
 
1. Attachments to streetlight poles 
2. Attachments to utility poles and utility lines 
3. Freestanding wireless facility infrastructure 
 
An overview of each type is included on the following pages.
